## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship for a material. Temperature affects material stiffness, yield behavior, and potentially activates thermally-driven deformation mechanisms like creep or thermal softening.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small strain, isothermal elasticity)
- Thermoelastic stress: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T (linear elasticity with thermal stress contribution)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (nonlinear thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood type nonlinear stress-strain)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated power-law plasticity)
- Hollomon with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 * T)**c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature-dependent strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (flow stress with hardening and thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * (c2 * T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon * T (quadratic strain with cross-coupling)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * T * sinh(c1 * epsilon) (high-temperature creep-type relationship)
- Neo-Hookean hyperelastic with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * epsilon**3) (nonlinear elasticity with cubic correction)
- Thermal softening rational form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 * T + c2)**(-1) (inverse temperature dependence of flow stress)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Stress proportional to epsilon multiplied by a decreasing function of T, e.g., (c0 - c1*T)*epsilon or c0*epsilon*exp(-c1*T)
- Strain hardening saturation → Stress approaches a plateau via (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or epsilon/(epsilon + c) forms
- Thermally activated processes → Arrhenius-type exp(c0 * (c1*T)) factors multiplying mechanical response terms
- Thermal expansion / residual stress → Additive terms proportional to T or (T - c0) independent of strain
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T indicating that hardening rate depends on temperature
- Power-law creep signature → sigma appears as epsilon**n where n < 1 (strain hardening) or involves T in the exponent
- Material phase transitions → Abrupt changes in slope suggesting piecewise or sigmoidal transitions in T
- Compressive vs tensile asymmetry → Odd powers of epsilon (epsilon, epsilon**3) dominate symmetric response; even powers indicate asymmetry
